    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<div id="review_2203610039" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2203610039" />
    <a title="Cracked Spine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74581846-cracked-spine"><img alt="Cracked Spine" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2203610039?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cracked Spine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cracked Spine" href="/user/show/74581846-cracked-spine">Cracked Spine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2203610039" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15501513611129470619">Jeffery M. Camp’s ‘Is Goat Beef?’ is a collection of the author’s favorite recipes along with his real life stories from when he was serving in the army. Not something you see side-by-side everyday, but it seems to work in this book. He wasn’t an army cook, he just shares his journeys and his enjoyment of food and drink, simply, in an upfront way that is both amusing and enlightening. The title hints that this isn’t a typically bland cookery book, but a publication offering a little bit more. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText15501513611129470619" style="display:none">Jeffery M. Camp’s ‘Is Goat Beef?’ is a collection of the author’s favorite recipes along with his real life stories from when he was serving in the army. Not something you see side-by-side everyday, but it seems to work in this book. He wasn’t an army cook, he just shares his journeys and his enjoyment of food and drink, simply, in an upfront way that is both amusing and enlightening. The title hints that this isn’t a typically bland cookery book, but a publication offering a little bit more. This is for readers who like something different, slightly left of center and irreverent. I enjoyed this book despite not being a fan of cookery or even interested in the military. The sheer implausibility of such a book existing, along with the intriguing title drew me in and made me curious and I’m glad I took the time to read it! </span>
  <a data-text-id="15501513611129470619" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2212233002" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8753098191849199988">A cookery book with a difference? An army veteran’s diary extracts? I’m not sure exactly where this fits but it’s certainly novel. An informal look at the lighter side of Jeffery M. Camp’s army experiences, with recipes thrown into the mix too. <br/><br/>Each recipe included here comes armed with information about why it was chosen as well as a bit of context, for instance the country the author was in at the time he learned it. There are photos too. Mostly of the final cooked products, but a few of his a</span>
  <span id="freeText8753098191849199988" style="display:none">A cookery book with a difference? An army veteran’s diary extracts? I’m not sure exactly where this fits but it’s certainly novel. An informal look at the lighter side of Jeffery M. Camp’s army experiences, with recipes thrown into the mix too. <br /><br />Each recipe included here comes armed with information about why it was chosen as well as a bit of context, for instance the country the author was in at the time he learned it. There are photos too. Mostly of the final cooked products, but a few of his army life to boot. <br /><br />The content of Camp’s book does strike this reader as a pair of unlikely bedfellows, but then again why not write about and combine two things you are passionate about and have experience of? Maybe there should be more difficult-to-shelve books out there! This reader put aside their doubts and enjoyed this book anyway!<br /></span>

    <a title="8th Day Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74583594-8th-day-reads"><img alt="8th Day Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512397836p2/74583594.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2203646840" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2023403165726547554">What an unusual, innovative book! With poetry, recipes with anecdotal prefaces and self-confessed digressions, this is pretty whimsical and that’s what made me enjoy it. Make no mistake though, the main servings of this book are recipes and military stories, side by side (some somewhat inexplicably). I learned some interesting insights into army life thanks to this book. Jeffery M.Camp writes in a conversational, upbeat way, throwing in snippets of education too, including foreign customs and la</span>
  <span id="freeText2023403165726547554" style="display:none">What an unusual, innovative book! With poetry, recipes with anecdotal prefaces and self-confessed digressions, this is pretty whimsical and that’s what made me enjoy it. Make no mistake though, the main servings of this book are recipes and military stories, side by side (some somewhat inexplicably). I learned some interesting insights into army life thanks to this book. Jeffery M.Camp writes in a conversational, upbeat way, throwing in snippets of education too, including foreign customs and language, gleaned from his time served overseas. Camp is a retired army officer so the stories are authentic and ‘straight from the horse’s mouth’. He even includes a glossary so you can become familiar with army acronyms and a conversion chart of measurements for the recipes. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2023403165726547554" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer629917377519675019">Is Goat Beef? was a quirky find, for sure. If you like food and drink recipes and have an interest in the army, you couldn’t ask for anything better!   <span id="freeText629917377519675019" style="display:none">Is Goat Beef? was a quirky find, for sure. If you like food and drink recipes and have an interest in the army, you couldn’t ask for anything better! It may be a niche interest book but it kept me entertained nonetheless.<br /><br />I felt like I’d almost took a tour of duty myself by the end of reading this. Camp taught me all kinds of wonderful things in addition to his recipes and ‘backstage’ army stories. He includes photographs of the dishes too – something I find invaluable when attempting to recreate culinary fea(s)ts.<br /><br />As simply a cookbook it would be uninspiring, I think. As a stand alone army memoir it would also be lacking and insubstantial, but by combining the two components Camp has produced something new and interesting.<br /><br /><br /></span>

In fact I would be interested to rea</span>
  <span id="freeText13615618234649145612" style="display:none">What an odd mix this book is, but somehow it really does work. The mix of stories from author Camp’s military background are a blend of profound, touching experience, and real laugh-out-loud funny. Personally I couldn’t imagine the level of commitment required for military service, but I really enjoyed this (albeit light-hearted) insight into that way of life. <br /><br />The writing was capable and certainly well handled and well paced for a memoir-esque book like this. In fact I would be interested to read something else by Camp if her ever decided to turn his hand to fiction. A book like that written along these lines I think could work very well.<br /></span>

      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uUC8JM2W98bAYvrnTzR7U2VUHVMKfPP/WqaKExwZf5lkBCc+adtwpuPKifMd/eo/achhT+NwejBBArMicG4k6w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Flazc3svIjeDjOSu0SRagROAwig9cu8PJz1/bf29Ke7LEihp32KlV6Akl7qD7cvtHxy+NNR+ZsA8mUZckcpynA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Stu reduces his airline flying schedule to train for triathlons, while Angie escapes the daily horrors of a prosecutor\'s job to pursue pro bono work. But death threats soon prove that the only thing Angie escaped was the protective arm of the District Attorney\'s office. All are at stake as the Pierces struggle to uncover the truth, both the enemy\'s, and their own. Sometimes the biggest enemy can be the one right next to you... FACE OF OUR FATHER is too literary to be a thriller, yet too thrilling to put down-a unique blend of action and intimacy-a thriller with a soul. How often does fiction change how we define integrity, prejudice, and evil?
